gefosforesceerd, gekwadreerd, Gold: 1, Pred: 1 || Yes, these Dutch words do form a perfect rhyme. 

In Dutch, as in many other languages, perfect rhymes are more common than in English. A perfect rhyme in a language with a stress accent is a rhyme where the vowels (and sometimes, as in the example, also the consonants) of two words are exactly the same. In effect, the stressed syllables in both words rhyme perfectly, irrespective of accent and of the rhythmic grouping. (Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfect_rhyme)</s>

In Dutch, the rhyme is established by the vowel sounds at the ends of the two words, which are both "ei" (as in "me"):

- "voorlieg" is pronounced "voor-LIEG"
- "ordenden" is pronounced "ohr-DEHN-den"

However, in the case of "voorlieg" and "ordenden," the stress is on the final syllable (lieg and den), but the vowel sounds "ei" create a perfect rhyme nonetheless.</s>
